The Sinking of the Dachang: Details 29

Crew Confirms Seven People Missing

Responsibility Issues Awaited Customs Investigation

The sinking of the Dahua Company's Dachang ship, which was hit by the Ping'an Company's export ship Dahua No. 1 outside the Wusong mouth on the evening of the day before yesterday at 8:30 PM, was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Here are the details obtained yesterday:

The Incident

On the evening of the day before yesterday (the 14th) at 8:30 PM, the Dachang ship was carrying 600 tons of coal from the Zhongxing Coal Mine Company and about 60-70 passengers to Shanghai from Dabu. At that time, when it was about 20 miles away from the Wusong mouth, at the second river, it saw the Dahua ship exporting and heading straight for it. The Dachang immediately sounded the horn and steered north to avoid it, but it was hit by the bow of the Dahua ship, resulting in a major disaster.

Captain Sought Help

In order to avoid the Dahua ship, the Dachang ship's bow had turned north, causing it to be hit hard on the starboard side of the waist by the Dahua. The engine room was directly hit, and after the hole was penetrated, water immediately flooded in and gradually sank. The captain, Yi Renbake (transliteration) (NBOYKO), saw that the ship had been hit and planned to steer the ship to the shore for easy rescue, but the machine was damaged and the rudder was ineffective, so he dropped anchor and sent up flares for help. After causing the accident, the Dahua continued to move forward due to the darkness of the night. After seeing the flares for help, it turned around to provide assistance.

Rescue Situation

When the accident happened, there were no other ships entering or leaving. Although rockets were launched, no ships responded. At about 9 PM, the Dahua returned and approached the anchor, and lowered several sampans. The crew and passengers of the Dachang were able to cross over to the ship one after another, about 100 people. By that time, it was about 10 o'clock, and the Dachang had completely sunk. The Dahua then returned to Wusong and sailed to Shanghai yesterday morning. The victims landed at the South City Wharf.

Passengers Rescued

In addition to carrying coal, the ship also had 60-70 passengers, most of whom were extremely poor. Some were homeless and came to Shanghai to seek work. About 30-40 people were rescued, so after arriving in Shanghai, they all left the ship and went elsewhere without reporting to the company. As a result, the exact number of people rescued and lost is still unknown.

Crew Inspection

The ship had a total of 64 crew members. In addition to those who escaped, the missing included comprador Pang Jinquan, second comprador Wang Yongyao, third helmsman Wang Pinsheng, carpenter Chen Pigen, stoker Xu Qinglan, oiler Yun Ren, and cook Tian Lai, totaling seven people.

Aftermath Arrangements

The crew members who were rescued and arrived in Shanghai reported to the company and inquired about the aftermath arrangements. Yan, the wife of carpenter Chen Pigen, also came to the company and demanded to see her husband, crying and stamping her feet. Despite the persuasion of others, she was still ineffective. As a result, the staff were unable to handle the matter. Later, Yao Zhongxuan, a staff member, gave the head of the sailors, Tang, 75 yuan and ordered him to distribute 5 yuan to each of the sailors as temporary food and lodging expenses. The workers were not convinced by the verbal agreement, so Yao wrote a written acknowledgement before they dispersed. Chen Pigen's wife, Yan, was still not convinced, but after persuasion from Min Xinwu, the owner of the Tongde ship, she took 5 yuan and left.

Negotiation Procedures

After the owner reported the sinking of the Dachang, the Dahua Company sent a letter to the Customs and the Shipping Association and entrusted lawyer Xi Yuchang to conduct negotiations. The Ping'an Company also hired a lawyer. Yesterday, there were letters exchanged to serve as notification, but the issue of losses has not yet been raised.

Responsibility Issues

The responsibility for the collision between the Dahua and the Dachang was investigated by the Guowen News Agency reporter from both sides, each holding its own view. According to the Dachang, the ship saw the green light of the Dahua and immediately avoided it at an angle of 120 degrees. At that time, if the Dahua could have also avoided it slightly to the right, the collision would not have occurred. However, the ship went straight ahead without avoiding it, causing its bow to hit the abdomen of the Dachang ship, which was beyond rescue. According to the Dahua, the ship saw that the ship was close and immediately braked and sounded the distress signal four times. However, the incoming ship did not brake, but instead wanted to go around the left side of the Dahua's bow to go faster, causing its abdomen to touch our bow. The accounts of events are different, making it difficult to prove who is right and wrong. It is expected that after a thorough investigation by the Customs, the truth will be revealed.

Brief History of the Two Ships

The Dachang ship is owned by the Dahua Company at 41 Gongguan Road in this city, with a load capacity of 1,600 tons. It was built years ago and is used exclusively for cargo. From the 25th of last month, it was leased to the Zhongxing Coal Mine Company and declared through the Xincheng Honest Broker Company in Yuelai Company on Hankou Road. It traveled between Dabu and Shanghai, specializing in carrying coal. After Zhongxing took over, it only traveled twice before the accident occurred. The losses will be included in the Dachang negotiations. The ship was insured by the Dahua Company for 50,000 taels at the Hua'an Company, but it is less than half of the loss. The Dahua ship is a Dinghai-class ship of the Ping'an Company, with a load capacity of 600 tons. After colliding with the Dachang the night before yesterday, it rescued more than 100 people. It returned to Shanghai yesterday morning. Because the bow was also slightly injured, it was temporarily suspended for repairs. All passengers and cargo will be transferred to the Chuanshan ship today.

Retrieving Bodies

In addition to rescuing more than 100 crew members and passengers, there are still 40-50 people missing. In order to retrieve the bodies, the company sent a letter to the Wusong Rescue Bureau yesterday, requesting to retrieve them and offering a reward of 40 yuan per body. The letter to the Rescue Bureau said, "We hereby inform you that the Dachang ship was sunk by the Dahua ship outside the Wusong mouth at 8:30 PM last night. In addition to those who escaped, seven crew members of the Dachang ship are still missing. We hereby ask your bureau to search for them everywhere. If any bodies are found that match the names of the crew members, a reward of 40 yuan will be given to each body, which will be paid by our company according to the list. We will not go back on our word. We hereby inform you and hope you will investigate and handle the matter."

Yesterday 30

Annual Meeting of Western Taxpayers

All Seven Resolutions Passed

Purchase of the Great China Hotel Rejected

The annual meeting of Western taxpayers in the Public Settlement was held at the Great Guangming Theater at 2:00 PM yesterday. Mr. Macnaghten, Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Council, presented eight resolutions prepared by the Municipal Council to the meeting for voting. First, Mr. Baker was elected as the chairman of the annual meeting, and Mr. Lyell was appointed as the secretary. Within one hour, all seven resolutions were passed. When discussing the eighth resolution regarding the purchase of the Great China Hotel, the atmosphere became tense. The resolution was proposed by Mr. Harris and seconded by Mr. Fessenden. After the discussion began, five people spoke against it, and one person spoke in favor. The matter was then put to a vote, and it was ultimately rejected by a majority. The Municipal Council's plan to purchase the Great China Hotel, which had attracted attention from various sectors, was thus defeated. The meeting adjourned at 3:40 PM. The details of the meeting are recorded below:

After the first, second, and third resolutions, which were the election of the chairman and secretary, and the adoption of the meeting rules, were completed, Chairman Macnaghten proposed:

Resolution Four: "To pass the municipal report and final accounts for the year ending December 31, 1930." Mr. Macnaghten delivered a report on the proposal, stating that the various municipal affairs handled by the Municipal Council last year had been detailed in the annual report. He would like to add a few words on the more important matters. He hoped that everyone would remember that in June of the previous year, the Municipal Council hired Mr. Craig to assist in implementing the recommendations of the Economy Committee and to join the work of the Salary Committee as secretary. By June of last year, the Salary Committee had submitted a report that was grand in scope and comprehensive in planning. The Municipal Council adopted it after making only a few minor changes, which were still in line with the committee's intentions, but only with different methods. The Municipal Council now has a comprehensive salary scale based solely on merit for promotion. The committee had suggested opening up avenues for Chinese staff to serve in positions with heavier responsibilities, and the Municipal Council expressed its strong agreement. In the future, the policy of hiring will be to employ Westerners only when no suitable Chinese staff can be found. The Municipal Council firmly believes that adopting the Salary Committee's report will greatly benefit the economy of government expenditures. He expressed his gratitude to the committee members for their diligent service to the public. In addition, Mr. Craig also formulated implementation measures for the Salary Committee's recommendations and made many improvements to the Municipal Council's rules of procedure. In the past, the management and authority of municipal affairs were concentrated in the hands of the Director-General. Now, with the development of the region and the increasing complexity of municipal affairs, there is inevitably a risk of administrative overload and slow processing. Mr. Craig has now revised the responsibilities of the heads of various departments to match the increased responsibilities. He has also assembled several departments to form several joint committees to directly handle matters related to those departments, thereby avoiding the trouble of the Director-General's office serving as a hub for consultations and document exchanges. In this way, the efficiency of management is not hindered, personnel are greatly saved, and administration is greatly expedited. In addition, he has also revised the rules of procedure for the Board of Directors, committees, and various departments, eliminating the past defects of unclear responsibilities. Future administration will be greatly facilitated. Mr. Craig completed all of the above arduous work in March. The Board of Directors was completely satisfied, and the Municipal Council and the public benefited greatly. At last year's annual meeting of taxpayers, there was the most pessimistic

commentary on the Shanghai Special District Court.

Some Western newspapers also created a widespread impression abroad that the abolition of the Provisional Court and its replacement with the Special District Court was tantamount to a disaster, and that the rights of Westerners and the protection of Western interests were sacrificed for political expediency. Today, I am very happy to inform you that the Special District Court has been very effective in handling criminal cases over the past year. The doubts that Westerners had a year ago have now been dispelled in nine out of ten cases. As you all know, the security and order in the settlement are greatly influenced by the criminal administration of the Special District Court. Last year, the Municipal Council filed charges in a total of 20,883 criminal cases, large and small, of which 19,457 people were convicted and 1,426 were acquitted. In light of the situation in Shanghai, this can be regarded as a record that surpasses the administration of criminal courts in various countries. In addition, there is very little dissatisfaction with the Special District Court's enforcement of criminal law. However, there was no progress on the

issue of road construction beyond the boundaries, which is a pity. Until recently, a method was agreed upon with the local Chinese authorities, and it is hoped that this will allow the road surface to be maintained and repaired from time to time. As for the telephone issue, the Shanghai Telephone Company's purchase of the business property of the China and Foreign Telephone Company was signed into a contract with the Municipal Council on August 5th of last year, obtaining a franchise to quickly rectify the situation and completely renovate the automatic telephone system within two years. Only after this has been completed will it be allowed to increase telephone fees. At the end of February of this year, the company reported on the progress of its work. 43,000 automatic telephones ordered from two factories of the International Telephone and Telegraph Corporation have been 60% delivered and are currently being installed in fully completed switchboards. The buildings on Bixun Road and Tilanqiao have been completed, the one on Fujian Road is about to be completed, the one on Mintinein Road is 90% completed, and the two in the West and North districts are also 85% completed. The wiring project has created 152 manholes and buried 1,411,000 feet of pipe, laying 572,400 feet of underground and aerial cable, with a total length of 56,450 miles of telephone lines. However, the renovation of new equipment outside the settlement is often interfered with by the Chinese authorities, and the Municipal Council has approved the exemption of its obligations under the contract for roads outside the boundaries.

The Municipal Council's final accounts and accounting report for last year

have already been published, and I will now add a few words on several key points. The surplus for last year was 2,271,000 taels, a decrease of more than 1 million taels compared to the budget of 3,277,000 taels. The reason for this has been detailed in the accounting report, and the fall in the price of silver was the biggest reason. Last year, the cost of the police force accounted for 16% of the total revenue. The adoption of several recommendations of the Salary Committee has increased the cost of security, with Chinese police officers benefiting the most. However, although this cost is huge, the public has benefited from it, and I believe that everyone will agree with this. As for the

promotion of education, the revenue used for education last year accounted for 4.6% (excluding investment expenditures). However, since the adoption of the Education Committee's recommendations, the percentage will increase significantly from this year onwards. The Municipal Council currently runs a total of 13 schools, 7 of which educate Chinese children and 6 of which educate foreign children. At the end of last year, there were a total of 3,281 Chinese students, but many students were not able to be admitted due to insufficient school buildings. There were a total of 1,536 foreign students, and several schools have ample space to accommodate more people. As for the addition of a new school for Western children in the West District, although no progress has been made, the Municipal Council is focusing all its efforts on hoping to take concrete steps soon. Since the establishment of the Education Committee in June of last year, it has drafted procedures for expanding public schools and subsidizing private schools. The Municipal Council has already approved them in principle. In addition, there is one more point that I would like to draw your special attention to, which is the accounting report's description of the

disposition of the Electricity Department's sales.

Since the Municipal Council sold the Electricity Department, there has been a feeling that the city treasury has received such a large income that it can be taken without end and used without limit. Therefore, please pay special attention to this report to understand the truth and dispel erroneous impressions. I also want to tell you that if the Electricity Department had not been sold, the police donation and land tax would not only not be reduced, but would also increase to 20%. As for the special revenue and expenditure items, the surplus was 3,344,711 taels, an increase of approximately 962,000 taels compared to the budget of 2,382,700 taels. Last year, the Shanghai Electric Power Company paid a total purchase price of 23,500,000 taels, which the Municipal Council used to redeem ten types of municipal bonds (including the gold pound loan of 1920) and to pay for various investment expenditures. However, the original planned building construction program was not fully implemented, and a portion of the funds saved was allocated to cover the land purchase expenses required for widening roads, as there was an unusual development in the reconstruction of buildings within the boundaries that year, which led to a sharp increase in the cost of widening roads. I would now like to submit Resolution Four for your consideration. The chairman then put the resolution to a vote, and it was passed without dissent.

Resolution Five: "To approve the various expenditures in the 1931 budget prepared by the outgoing Board of Directors, as well as its accompanying recommendations, and to authorize the Municipal Council to collect the various taxes listed in the resolution." He also declared to the public that the budget for this year has an explanation attached, which compares the various revenues and expenditures of the current and previous years, so there is no need to repeat the details except for mentioning one or two of the important points. This year, the police donation on Chinese and foreign houses within the settlement will continue to be collected at 14% of the rent, as in the second half of last year, and 12% for those outside the settlement. The land tax will still be collected at 7 per thousand of the assessed value. The estimated surplus for the budget is 310,000 taels of silver, while the surplus for the previous year was 2,271,000 taels.

The current budget is sufficient to offset revenue and expenditure, and it is gratifying that there is no need to increase taxes this year. However, the surplus is too small, which is somewhat unsatisfactory. This may be due to the sharp drop in the price of silver, which has had a direct and indirect impact on various items in the budget. I remember that in my speech at last year's annual meeting, I said that the Municipal Council hoped to maintain the low tax rate for several years. Although the Municipal Council still has this hope, if the exchange rate does not make real progress in the near future, it may be necessary to restore the tax rate that was implemented before July of last year next year. Regarding this section, the public may not fully know that the taxes in Shanghai are approximately lower than those in any major city in Europe and the United States. For example, the United Kingdom often collects about 70% of the rent, and the municipal councils in the United Kingdom often receive subsidies from the government in addition to the municipal donations they collect to undertake certain public affairs. The estimated shortage for this year's special budget is 350,750 taels, while last year there was a surplus of 3,344,700 taels. This is due to the fact that special expenditures this year total 10 million taels, while the purchase price for the sale of the Electricity Department will be paid in installments over several years, and the amount payable this year is only 8 million taels.

The building construction program accounts for a large part of the special budget. Many buildings were included in last year's budget, but the work has not been completed and it is necessary to continue to allocate funds to complete them. The cost of imported building materials has risen due to the fall in the exchange rate, which is also a reason why the building construction program is more expensive. The policy of

purchasing land and widening roads at the appropriate time

is planned to be continued. Since the recent revaluation of land prices, the cost of widening roads has also increased significantly.

Under the item of debt repayment, it is stipulated that the 1931 8% public bond and the debt repayment fund will be stored in batches for the repayment of debts that cannot be redeemed before December 31, 1933, because the final installment of the purchase price of the Electricity Department must be paid on that day.

The procedures for the education policy, which were revised by the Education Committee and approved by the Municipal Council, have been announced and do not need to be repeated. They stipulate that two Chinese girls' middle schools will be established before 1934, and two co-educational Chinese children's primary schools will be built each year between this year and 1928. They also stipulate the procedures for subsidizing private Chinese and foreign schools that the Municipal Council deems should be assisted. According to this program, by the end of 1938, there will be 23 public Chinese children's schools in the settlement. It is estimated that by that time, the public schools will be able to accommodate approximately 7% of the Chinese children of school age in the settlement. The cost required for this program this year is a relatively small amount. It should be known that the Chinese education expenses that you are asked to approve today are still far different from the expenses for public Western children's schools, and the total amount of education expenses (including 150,000 taels allocated for subsidizing various schools) accounts for slightly less than 9% of the Municipal Council's revenue. You should know that in the future, taxpayers will be asked to gradually increase Chinese children's education expenses each year until 1938 (unless there are unforeseen events that prevent or accelerate our progress), when education expenses may account for approximately 16% of the Municipal Council's revenue. I dare to say that you will generously approve this year's expenses, because although the number of Chinese children far exceeds that of Western children, the benefits that they receive from the Municipal Council's stipulated education expenses this year are still only half of the total amount, so there is no reason to be stingy and disapprove them. Moreover, your approval today does not deprive future taxpayers of the right to stop the need. I firmly believe that future taxpayers will also be as enlightened as you and know that this settlement is responsible for contributing progressive educational opportunities to Chinese children within the settlement. In order for Chinese and foreign taxpayers to understand the expenses required for public education, the Municipal Council has decided to set up a separate item for the education budget in the municipal fee accounting. As for the method of raising education funds, whether it is from special donations or other means, it will be discussed in the future. After the declaration, the chairman put the resolution to a vote, and it was unanimously passed by the entire meeting.

Resolution Six: To elect one real estate committee member for this year, Robinson was elected.

Resolution Seven: To elect four annual directors of the Public Dispensary Hospital for this year, Dr. White, Dr. Deng, Cage, and Shepard were elected.

Resolution Eight: To propose the acquisition of the Great China property, the content of which is "to propose that the public acquire the Great China Hotel property for the citizens for use as a park and social hub, provided that the selling price is deemed reasonable by the Municipal Council and that the city treasury's financial resources can still open up necessary open spaces in densely populated areas for implementation. Please await the public's decision." It was proposed by Harris, who also gave a speech to the public, stating that the Municipal Council has not purchased open space for the people for seventeen years. During this period, the Municipal Council's income has increased threefold, and the sale of the Municipal Hall on Nanjing Road has also yielded 1.25 million taels, which is stored for the construction of a new Municipal Hall. Now the opportunity has arrived. If we miss it, it will be a great regret for the Municipal Council. The Great China Hotel is world-renowned and is also a source of pride for the Public Settlement. The Great China property is approximately 60 acres and has convenient transportation. What I propose is to convert the Great China Hotel into a Municipal Hall for annual meetings and concerts, and to build an art gallery and a library. The current dance hall will be preserved, and a swimming pool and an open-air movie theater will be opened. The Great China property is valued at 3.5 million taels, an average of 60,000 taels per acre. The land in its vicinity has now been sold for 125,000 taels per acre, twice the asking price of the Great China property. All the buildings of the Great China Hotel are not priced, so there is no sacrifice in renovation or preservation. There are now more than ten groups that support this proposal. The seconder, Mr. Fessenden, was then followed by Mr. Macnaghten, Chairman of the Municipal Council, who stated that the Municipal Council has published its opinion on this proposal in various newspapers. The Municipal Council firmly opposes this proposal because it believes that it is justified from the perspective of effective municipal administration. The first point that the Municipal Council considers when considering such events is, of course, whether the acquisition of a special property can benefit all residents. The Municipal Council always distinguishes between important and unimportant in any plan that involves the use of large sums of money, does what the public wants, and does not undertake things that are not necessary. The various arguments made by those who advocate the purchase of the Great China property are mostly motivated by emotion and treat the two ends of consolidated finances and interests indifferently. Therefore, it is undoubtedly an emotional effect that a large part of the residents expect to purchase the Great China property as a place for entertainment. There is no sufficient reason to use large sums of money to do this, and there is no real guarantee that the land will be permanently retained for public use for entertainment after it is acquired and developed in the future. Some people have suggested that the municipal organs can be moved there in the future and that some space can be left to serve as a so-called social center, park, or open space. It should be known that moving the municipal organs there is not suitable in terms of economy and practical benefits. This has already been detailed to the public and does not need to be

repeated. As for using it as a social center, it is not only too expensive and beyond our ability, but the land area is also insufficient. As for using it as a

Page 10

park and open space, it is also not suitable in terms of location and area. If this is done, it will only benefit a few relatively wealthy people and will still not be able to alleviate the urgent need for parks and open spaces in the densely populated areas of the settlement. Now, if the Great China property is acquired, the Municipal Council's plan to purchase land in densely populated areas to build parks will have to be abandoned. Moreover, once a large sum of 3.5 million taels is spent, the annual regular budget will increase the burden by approximately 250,000 taels, which may result in an increase in the police donation to make up for it. This is what we should try to avoid as much as possible. After Macnaghten finished his declaration, he asked the public to vote on the proposal. Fessenden immediately stood up to support Harris's opinion and gave a brief speech. Then Macnaghten stood up again to refute Harris's remarks that the Municipal Council had not purchased open space for taxpayers for seventeen years. Finally, he said that the Board of Directors of the Municipal Council had decided not to advocate the purchase of the Great China property. Next, Fukushima, the Japanese director, stood up to correct Harris's misunderstanding of several points in his speech. Next, Wilma, an American taxpayer, stood up to oppose the proposal, and her words were quite激昂, saying that she loved to dance, and the Great China was indeed a beautiful dance place. She knew that Harris also loved to dance, and she had often seen Harris enter and exit the place. However, the Municipal Council was not in the business of theaters, and we would not be affected if we did not have this entertainment venue. Next, Hayashi, the president of the Japanese Road Association, and Inoue, a Japanese taxpayer, spoke out against the proposal one after another. The proposal was then put to a vote, and it was rejected by a majority of opponents.

Starting May 1st 33

Ordering Foreign Fishing Vessels to Leave the Country

Maintaining the Livelihood of Fishermen

Preventing Japanese Aggression

According to reliable information, the National Government has ordered the Minister of Foreign Affairs, Wang Zhengting, to negotiate with the Japanese acting minister, Shigemitsu Aoi, because Japanese fishing vessels have recently been secretly arriving in our territorial waters to fish, harming the livelihood of our fishermen. The matter was resolved by the State Council, stating that since there is no special fishery agreement between China and Japan, the scope of our territorial waters cannot be the base for fishermen from that country, and they must be ordered to withdraw from our coast. After this matter was submitted for negotiation, the Japanese government sent a special envoy to China to negotiate, stating that the Chinese government had not previously prohibited it and that it was related to the livelihood of Japanese fishermen, and requested that it be maintained. It is heard that the authorities sternly rejected it, and the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs ordered the Jianghai Customs to order all foreign fishing vessels in China to withdraw from our coast starting on May 1st in order to maintain the livelihood of fishermen. After that, foreign fish imports will be treated as commodity transportation and must have a port of origin to prove that they are allowed to be imported. If anyone secretly sells foreign fish to our refrigerated ships, they will be punished.

Beijing-Shanghai Railway Freight Train 34

Derailed at Fenlu Station Last Night

Night Express Train Still Departed on Time

A freight train on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway heading eastbound derailed at Fenlu Station at 7:00 PM last night. One locomotive and five freight cars suddenly derailed. A rescue train was dispatched from Beijing Station to lift the derailed vehicles first, which will take approximately two hours this morning to repair. The westbound night express train still departed on time from a temporary sidetrack.

Regular Elections for Agricultural Education Groups

The register of representatives for the National Assembly's Shanghai County Education Association, Farmers' Association, and Free Professional Groups has been approved and returned by the Director-General of Jiangsu. Therefore, the strict director of this county has specially scheduled the election for the 20th of this month. The issued notices and announcements are recorded below:

(1) Notice: Regarding the matter of the notice, it has been found that the qualifications of the electors of the National Assembly's representatives for the county's Farmers' Association, Education Association, and Free Professional Groups have been approved and have been announced separately according to the register. Now, in accordance with the prescribed time limit, the Education Association will vote at the Fourth District Office. The Education Associations of the First, Second, Third, and Sixth Districts will vote at the Third District Office in Beiqiao. After the voting is completed, the ballots will be counted immediately. In addition to notifying the relevant parties, a notice is hereby issued for all electors to be informed. Special notice. The notice from the Lawyers' Association is roughly the same. The polling place is located at the association's office on Baylor Road in the French Concession. As for the Farmers' Associations in each district, the election will be held on the same day at the same polling place as the Education Association.

(2) Announcement: Regarding the matter of the announcement, it has been found that the qualifications of the electors of the National Assembly's representatives for the county's Education Association and Farmers' Association have been approved by the Director-General of Jiangsu Province and made into a register, which has been issued to the county. It should be announced immediately. After the announcement, if the person believes that there are errors or omissions, they should be limited to before April 19 to obtain a certificate and submit it for the Director-General to review and approve. Late submissions will not be forwarded. In addition to announcing the scheduled voting election separately, the names of the electors will be announced hereinafter in accordance with the approved register, and please pay attention to whether there are any errors or omissions and submit them within the time limit, and do not delay yourself. Sincerely, special notice.

Crop Expert 37

American Dr. Love Comes to China

Guiding the Improvement of Cotton, Rice, and Wheat in Jiangsu and Zhejiang

The former Ministry of Agriculture and Mining and the provincial governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang considered the improvement of crops in Jiangsu and Zhejiang to be extremely important to the people's livelihood and were eager to recruit experts to strive for improvement. Therefore, last year, they jointly hired Dr. Love, a world-renowned expert in crop improvement and a professor at Cornell University in the United States, to come to China to guide the improvement of cotton, rice, and wheat in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, and to serve concurrently as a senior agricultural advisor to the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining. The term of the contract is three years. After the merger of the Ministry of Agriculture, Mining, Industry, and Commerce into the Ministry of Industry, Minister Kong believed that Dr. Love was extremely famous in the United States, and that the number of agricultural talents he had taught in crop improvement was unmatched by any professor in the United States. He is recognized worldwide as the most famous crop expert and the first person to apply biochemistry to the American agricultural community. Therefore, he attached great importance to Dr. Love's arrival in China and sent a telegram to the United States to welcome him and urge him to come quickly. It is now heard that Dr. Love has boarded a ship to China and is expected to arrive in Shanghai around the 17th of this month. Minister Kong of the Ministry of Industry has specially sent Vice Minister Mu to welcome him in Shanghai, and will convene a meeting with representatives of the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces and crop experts from the two provinces to discuss Professor Love's work plan for crop improvement in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. His duties to the Ministry of Industry will be determined after he meets with Minister Kong in Beijing.

News of the Customs Workers' Strike Yesterday 45

Customs Brokers' Association to Convene Emergency Meeting Today

Since the Cotton Cloth Association announced the cancellation of cartage fees, etc., the workers in the customs brokerage industry in this city have launched a strike. Hat Making Industry Continues Strike 46

Union Officials Offer Resignations

The hat-making workers in this city have been on strike since the 5th, due to their opposition to the employers' abuse of apprenticeships and wage deductions. More than ten days have passed, and the matter remains unresolved. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau believes that the strike was launched without mediation and should be dealt with severely. Out of consideration for their ignorance, the workers were ordered to resume work by a certain date. However, the workers insisted on refusing because the dispute had not been properly resolved. Wang Yuxiang, Zhu Wenbiao, and ten other directors and supervisors of the Hat Makers' Union resigned from their positions to all members on the day before yesterday, and simultaneously submitted a report to the Party and government authorities for record. It is reported that as the weather is gradually getting hotter, fellow straw hat traders are deeply concerned that the prolonged strike will hinder business. Therefore, they have been holding meetings for several days to discuss the matter and have submitted a request to higher authorities for assistance.

Jinxin Factory 47

Workers Petition the Municipal Government Yesterday

The Jinxin Silk Weaving Factory on Avenue Haig in the French Concession has been on strike for more than twenty days. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has mediated six times, but the factory has been insincere, resulting in unsuccessful mediation. The matter was then submitted for arbitration. Yesterday, because they had not seen a clear written summons from the Municipal Government, more than three hundred workers gathered in front of the union hall and petitioned the Municipal Government. At that time, the Secretary-General of the Municipal Government came out to meet with them and promised to convene arbitration immediately, no later than Saturday. The workers felt that the result of the petition was satisfactory and dispersed happily.

Marine Engineers Association 49

Declaration Regarding Zheng Zhensheng's Death in Prison

Requesting Assistance from All Sectors

Seaman Zheng Zhensheng was arrested in 1925 for helping with the May Thirtieth Strike and plotting to assassinate Wang Chongqing, the foreman of the Yinying Company. He was detained in the Western Prison for five years. He suddenly died in the Western Prison on February 25 of this year. After hearing the news, his wife, Ms. Chai, went to the Seamen's Union to seek redress. The union immediately submitted a report to the central government, which in turn instructed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Industry to negotiate on the matter. More than a month has passed, and there is still no progress. Recently, marine engineers have organized the Marine Engineers Association to support Zheng's case and seek redress. The association has issued a declaration, excerpts of which are as follows: "Our fellow seaman and martyr, Zheng Zhensheng, responded with righteous indignation after the May Thirtieth Massacre. He contacted all fellow seamen and launched a strike in support of the nation. Unexpectedly, the foreman Wang Chongqing obstructed the strike. Zheng Zhensheng disregarded his own safety and went directly to his residence to eliminate this menace to the revolutionary cause. However, he failed to achieve his goal and suffered misfortune first. His gun malfunctioned, leading to his arrest and false accusation of robbery and murder. He was sent to the Joint Court for trial. Zheng Zhensheng, still thinking of preserving the reputation of his Ningbo hometown and avoiding implicating his comrades, changed his name from Zheng Fangren, using Fangren, claiming to be from Tanggu. He was sentenced to imprisonment in the Western Prison for five years. As the term was nearing its end, our colleagues and the Seamen's Union repeatedly requested the National Government to negotiate for his release, but the concession authorities, based on consular jurisdiction, required another ten years, creating a stalemate. Recently, Zheng Zhensheng's family suddenly received word from the prison that Zheng Zhensheng had died in prison. According to the date, more than twenty days have passed. The cause of death remains unknown, and he died in prison with grievance and hatred. The news was shocking and caused great suspicion. In addition to the three measures proposed by the Seamen's Union to the central government, we hereby issue a declaration, respectfully requesting assistance from all sectors to redress the wrongs done to Zheng Zhensheng and to uphold justice. We hereby declare this."

Ningbo People 50

Incensed by the French Police Injuring a Person

Xin Haishan was shot and injured by a French constable without cause. After being sent to Renji Hospital for treatment, the Western doctors at the hospital reported that his injuries were very serious and life-threatening. After hearing the news, Ningbo people in Shanghai flocked to the Ningbo Native Place Association, demanding negotiations. They all said that the barbaric actions of the French police had aroused great anger. The association is prepared to submit another request to the authorities for serious negotiations and to punish the Western constable according to the law in order to appease the people. Furthermore, the Seafood Trade Association sent a telegram regarding the case of Xin Haishan being shot by the French police: "To the Shanghai Municipal Government, the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the French Municipal Council, the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the French Concession, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, the Ningbo Native Place Association in Shanghai, the various trade associations, and all organizations and newspapers: Our association's member, Xin Haishan, a clerk at Changhe Firm, was shot without cause by Western constable No. 158 of the French police on the 7th of this month at 9 PM while going out on business. The bullet entered from the lower part of the left jaw and went straight through the neck, causing him to fall to the ground unconscious. The Western constable and his Yue policeman colleague immediately moved Xin's body to the side alley of Puanli, hoping to shirk responsibility and escape. At that time, Li Dexuan from Tianjin, who was passing by, witnessed the situation, filled with righteous indignation, and immediately recorded the number of the Western constable. The Chinese policeman in the alley reported the matter to the French police station by telephone, and a car was sent to Renji Hospital for treatment. Changhe Firm then appealed to our association and sent separate letters to the Native Place Association, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the French Concession, which were forwarded to the local government for submission to the French consul for negotiations. This case occurred nearly ten days ago. Xin Haishan's injuries are serious and he is on the verge of death. Even if he recovers, he will be disabled. How will his eight-member family make a living? It is difficult to predict whether the French consul will punish the Western constable No. 158 according to the law and compensate the victim for all losses. However, the French police station has not yet filed a public prosecution and has not shown any intention of punishing the perpetrator or providing compensation. Such indifference clearly shows that the police are protecting the Western constable and disregarding the lives of Chinese people. It is not an exaggeration to say that they are encouraging the constable to commit murder. The purpose of establishing a police force in the concession is to protect the area and safeguard merchants. Now, the Western constable has violated his own duties and dared to trample on merchants and harm good people. Are they using the concession as a shield to disregard human life and ignore the law? Our association cannot bear to sit idly by while a fellow trader's clerk is brutally harmed. We should, based on the facts, telegraphically request those who uphold humanity to seriously negotiate and achieve the goals of punishing the perpetrator, providing compensation, and ensuring that such incidents do not occur again in the future. The matter concerns national dignity and the lives of the people. We beg you to uphold justice, rise up, and provide support. Urgent telegram, awaiting your orders. Hu Xing, chairman of the Shanghai Seafood and Grocery Trade Association."

Local News II

Nanjing Road 53

A Battle with Robbers Last Night

Robbers Commit Robbery on Xin Zha Road

Wang Yongtai Loses Several Hundred Dollars

Detectives and Robbers Exchange Fire

Resulting in Deaths and Injuries on Both Sides

Wang Yongtai Shoe Store, located at No. 1986 Xin Zha Road, was in the process of closing up last night around 10 PM when seven robbers suddenly arrived. Each of them produced a handgun and robbed over two hundred dollars and a silver watch before leaving. Detectives discovered this and pursued them to the corner of Xizang Road and Nanjing Road, where they exchanged gunfire. One robber was killed, and another was captured. One police officer was injured, and three bystanders were hit by stray bullets. The details are as follows:

Seven Robbers Commit Robbery at Wang Yongtai Shoe Store. The store is owned by Wang Yisheng from Pudong. It is a single-frontage store with eight or nine clerks and apprentices. They were finishing work and closing up when seven robbers suddenly rushed into the store. Six of them were wearing long gowns, and one was wearing a short gown. They each produced handguns and forced the clerks and apprentices to a corner upstairs, forbidding them from looking directly at them and from making any noise. The robbers then proceeded to rob the store for about ten minutes before heading east. It is estimated that they stole over two hundred dollars and a silver watch.

Alert Detectives. After the robbers fled with their loot, a detective from the Xin Zha Police Station happened to be passing by. He noticed that the Wang Yongtai store was wide open and there was no one inside. He also saw six or seven people rushing out, which aroused his suspicion. He immediately entered the store and asked the clerks if those were robbers. At that time, the clerks, still startled, were afraid to speak frankly. Later, an apprentice blurted out that it was a robbery. The detective immediately turned back and secretly pursued them, following them along Xin Zha Road to North Ni Cheng Bridge, then turning into Xizang Road. Upon reaching the opposite side of the New World, he saw a patrolman from the Lao Zha Police Station, No. 1400. Seeing that the opportunity had arrived, he quickly informed the patrolman, and together they drew their guns and fired. The robbers also returned fire.

Gunfire and Fighting. The confrontation occurred at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Xizang Road, around 10:30 PM, when there were many pedestrians passing by. Gunfire erupted, and pedestrians scrambled for cover. One robber was hit in the left hand and was captured. The remaining robbers turned east onto Nanjing Road and continued to fire as they fled. The detectives continued to pursue them relentlessly. The robbers fled to the front of the Great East Straw Hat Company at No. 641 Nanjing Road. The detectives pursued them to the front of the Washington Watch Store on the north side and exchanged fire across the street, firing more than ten shots. One robber was killed on the spot. Chinese patrolman Ma Changjun, No. 1400, was also hit in the left shoulder. The remaining robbers took the opportunity to escape.

Bystanders Affected. Zhang Dewei (from Ningbo, resident of No. 21 Jie Jin Fang, Kandi Road) was hit in the left foot by a stray bullet. Xu Peigen (from Jiangyin, resident of Huanghe Road, Da Tie Bang, a barber) was hit in the left arm. Shao Rulin (16 years old, from Nantong), an apprentice at the Great East Company, was sleeping on a camp bed in the store when a stray bullet penetrated the store and hit his left big toe. Furthermore, nine holes were pierced in the glass doors and windows of the Great East Company by stray bullets. The injured police officer was sent to the police hospital for treatment. Xu, Zhang, and Shao were all sent to Renji Hospital for treatment. Their injuries were not serious.

Three Convicts, including Taibao Ashu 54

Executed by Decapitation this Morning

Supervised by District Chief Xu

Escorted to Zhangyan for Execution

The bandit leaders Taibao Ashu, Xu Tianxiong, and his younger brother Xu Fusheng, Shengfeng Zhuzai, A Mei, and Wang Qiming, who were involved in robberies in eight counties including Songjiang, Qingpu, Jinshan, Fengxian, and Wujiang, have been sentenced to death and decapitation. The execution was scheduled for 10 AM today (the 16th) in Zhangyan Town, Jinshan County. Xu Pucheng, the district chief of the First District of the Jiangsu River Police stationed in Minhang, was ordered to supervise the execution. He had already ordered Detective Captain Huan Guanlin to come to Shanghai to recruit Wang Fusheng, who had been an executioner during the era of the former warlords, to prepare for the execution. He led a large patrol team and all the detectives, escorting the three convicts from Minhang on two small steamers to Zhangyan for strict deployment. The execution was carried out at the appointed time.

Car Dealers Request Careful Review of Vehicle Permits 55

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday received a letter from the Human-Powered Vehicle Trade Association regarding the Careful Review of Human-Powered Vehicle Permit Applications and submitted it to the Municipal Government. The petition stated that on the 14th of this month, the Human-Powered Vehicle Trade Association submitted a letter stating that the Municipal Government's 177th municipal meeting had decided to expand the number of human-powered vehicles in the Chinese area to 10,000. The measures were announced on the 11th of this month by the Municipal Finance and Public Utilities Bureaus. Out of the 10,000 vehicles, 7,400 were from the original existing vehicles in Shanghai South Gate and Zhabei, and 1,000 were reserved for Pudong, and 200 were reserved for eliminated three-wheeled vehicles, totaling 1,400 new vehicles. The purpose of increasing the number of human-powered vehicles was to show compassion to the poor and help the coolies. However, how to increase the number of vehicles in order to benefit the poor is a matter that should be considered. If the applicants for new vehicles are indeed coolies and poor people, the number should be increased accordingly to fulfill the original intention of helping the poor. However, in reality, there are many unscrupulous merchants and vehicle vendors among those applying for new vehicles. These vendors sell their existing vehicles to others and then purchase new vehicles to profit from speculative buying and selling. These unscrupulous merchants already own a large number of vehicles and are seeking to manufacture new vehicles to monopolize the market and exploit the coolies. This dangerous intention not only contradicts the original intention of the Municipal Government to empathize with the poor, but will also have a great impact on vehicle merchants and drivers. The measures for increasing the number of vehicles by the Finance and Public Utilities Bureaus stipulate that the registered vehicles should be reviewed. The association submitted a request to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward it to the Municipal Government and the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, requesting a careful review of the applications and a precise and detailed investigation to prevent unscrupulous merchants from deceiving the authorities and to fulfill the original intention of helping the poor and maintaining the livelihoods of vehicle merchants and drivers. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has determined that the measures for increasing the number of operating human-powered vehicles in the Chinese area have been announced by the Finance and Public Utilities Bureaus, and all those engaged in the human-powered vehicle business should comply with them. The association believes that the intention of increasing the number of vehicles this time is not from the general coolie drivers, but rather speculative means by vehicle vendors to monopolize the market, and requests a precise investigation during the legal review to avoid deception by unscrupulous merchants. The matter is legitimate and should be submitted to the Municipal Government for review. The Municipal Bureau is requested to investigate and conduct a careful review to ensure fairness and benefit the public.

Visited this Newspaper Yesterday

Englishman Locke Hardt, renowned worldwide as a writer, traveler, and photographer, recently traveled to the Far East to collect materials for the London Illustrated News and the Chicago Tribune's affiliated Pacific and Atlantic Photographic Society. Locke Hardt's Disappearance (Taken by this newspaper)

The Qu Chengqing Case 57

Kidnapper Leader Shi Arong Detained

Various Kidnappers Describe the Situation at the Time

Arong Cunningly Denies, Claiming He is Being Falsely Accused

Qu Chengqing, a Shanghai resident living at No. 1760 Hainin Road, was kidnapped in January of last year. A ransom of 100,000 gold pieces was demanded. Subsequently, the Wayside Police rescued Qu from the bandit's lair and captured eight kidnappers. After a thorough investigation by the Special District Court, they were convicted. Zhang Zhangji and Wang Qinen were both sentenced to death, but the sentences have not yet been carried out. The remaining six bandits, including He Qingen, were given various prison terms. However, the ringleader of the gang, identified by the bandits as Yong native Shi Arong, had fled and his whereabouts were unknown, making it impossible to arrest him. He was finally apprehended by detectives at No. 339 Tangshan Road the other day. Yesterday morning, he was brought before Judge Feng at the Special Court for questioning. The police also brought in other accomplices from the West Prison to testify. However, Qu Chengqing's residence has since been moved, making it impossible to summon him to court. According to Wang Yuqing's testimony, he first met Shi Arong in October of the year before last. After kidnapping Qu, they hid him in Shi's house in Runde Lane, Gongping Road. The ransom letters were also written at Shi's direction. Wang Afu testified that the defendant, Shi Arong, and the fugitive Bao Laoer and others kidnapped Qu on Hainin Road and put him in a car driven by Laoer to Shi's house, where he was hidden upstairs. He was given a gun and told to guard him. Zhang Zhangzhang testified that he was Bao Laoer's apprentice and was told by Bao and Shi to help on Hainin Road. Shen Adi also testified that he helped guard the hostage upstairs in Shi's house. When he tried to escape, he was slapped by Shi. Wang Qinen testified that Bao was his master and Shi was his master's younger brother. He was invited to help kidnap Qu and was later ordered to guard the hostage. Gui Kangsong also testified that he guarded the hostage in Shi's house. When questioned, Shi Arong claimed to have previously worked as an assistant for Detective Wu and vehemently denied any involvement in the kidnapping. He claimed that the statements of the other criminals were all false accusations. Judge Feng then ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and Wang Yuqing and the others to be returned to prison for further questioning at a later date.

What Are Sun Runwang's Intentions?

Chen Mutao 61

Recounts the Details of Embezzlement

Summarizing What He Said, He Was Burdened by His Younger Brother

Younger Brother Also Imprisoned for Another Case

After Giving a Detailed Account, He Collapses

The Court Orders Sentencing Next Wednesday

Chen Mutao of Jiahe has been working at the Zhejiang Industrial Bank for fourteen years, rising to the important position of Deputy Director of the Savings Department. Recently, he successively embezzled 64,000 yuan from savings deposits. Deeply worried that the matter would be exposed in the future, making it difficult to escape serious punishment, he left a letter and fled on the first day of this month, going alone to Wusong.

Hoping to Drown Himself in the Sea Late at Night, He Was Unexpectedly Stopped by the Iron Railing by the Riverbank

Unable to Pass, He Fell to the Ground. The Sleeping Pills He Took Took Effect, Causing Him to Faint. He Was Discovered by Someone, Who Carried Him to the Shanghai Public Hospital. The Police, Upon Receiving a Complaint from the Bank Regarding Embezzlement, Sent a Detective to Transfer Chen to the Labour Bureau Hospital for Treatment. After Recovery, He Was Taken to the Special District Court. The Interrogation Had Already Been Reported by This Newspaper. Yesterday Morning, Presiding Judge Xu Jiashi Continued the Trial in the First Court. The Police Lawyer, Ru Bao-I,

Repeated the Case Once Again. The Zhejiang

Industrial Bank Retained Lawyer Wu Shou-Gong to Clearly State That in Addition to the Public Prosecution by the Police, Zhejiang Industry Must Also File a Civil Suit, Requesting a Judgment Ordering the Repayment of the Embezzled Funds. The Defendant Retained Lawyer Jiang Bao-Lian to Defend Him. Subsequently, Chen Xuanzhen, Manager of the Bank, Appeared in Court and Stated, That Chen Mutao Had Been Working for Ten Years, Extremely Honest and Capable. The Savings Department Was Organized With a Director, Deputy Director, and Three Team Leaders. Chen Was

The Head of the Three Team Leaders. The Team Leader Was

The Head of One Group, In Charge of The Receipt and Payment of Funds. When the Deputy Director Was Unable to Serve for Any Reason, Chen Would Take His Place. Chen Began to Use His Position as Acting Deputy Director to Embezzle Funds Since Autumn of the Eighteenth Year. The Amount He Has Been Found to Have Embezzled Is 64,000 Yuan. Whether There Were Other Malpractices Is Yet to Be Discovered. The Reason Why This Was Discovered Now Is Because Chen Was Officially Promoted to Deputy Director and Took Office on March 1. He Realized That the Embezzled Accounts Would Be Exposed at the End of the Month, So He Fled on April 1. However, We Initially Did Not Know About The Embezzlement Until

He Was Rescued After Attempting Suicide by Poison in Wusong

. The Police Searched Him and Found a Letter, Which Revealed The Truth. He Presented The Account Books To The Court and Asked It To Investigate. At This Time, The Defendant, Chen Mutao, Requested The Judge To Allow Him to Recount the Details of The Misappropriation and All of His Hardships. Judge Xu Granted The Request. Chen Then Began to Describe The Situation, Saying That He Had Studied Poetry and Had Some Knowledge of Propriety. His Beloved Mother Passed Away When He Was Seventeen Years Old. Before Her Death, She Repeatedly

Instructed Him to Protect and Care For His Younger Brother. He Did Not Dare To Forget This.

Therefore, This Matter Was Due to Caring for His Younger Brother. He Was Introduced to The Xinhua Bank By Friends and Relatives When He Was Nineteen Years Old. He Soon Became Ill and Resigned. He Was Introduced to The Zhejiang Industrial Bank When He Was Twenty Years Old and Has Been Working There Ever Since. He Has Been There for Fourteen Years. He Knew That He Had Always Been Diligent and Harmonious With His Colleagues and Servants. He Was Greatly Affected by The Student Protests in The Past. He Also Liked to Read Novels, Especially "Romance of The Three Kingdoms."

He Admired Liu, Guan, and Zhang The Most. Over Time, He Was Subconsciously

Influenced By The Heroes in The Novel. Therefore, He Tried His Best to Help Anyone Who Asked For Help. Even If He Could Not Afford It, He Would Find a Way to Help. In the Eighteenth Year, My Younger Brother, Cici,

Opened Jinkang Foreign Goods Company in My Father's Name. He Managed it Poorly and Made Friends With Bad Company. As a Result, He Often Went to Gambling Dens Day and Night. He Lost A Lot of Money. He Would Come To Me and Say That He Needed Money to Order Goods and Ask Me to Temporarily Advance Him The Funds. I Did Not Know That He Was Spending It On Gambling, So I Repeatedly Helped Him, Resulting In

A Total Advance of More Than 10,000 Gold. When Jinkang Closed

, Creditors Pressured Him. I Again Repaid More Than 10,000 Yuan of Debt. In Addition, I Helped Countless Numbers of My Younger Brother's Gambling Friends. I Spent So Much That I Could Not Afford It. In June of Last Year, My Younger Brother's Creditor, Huacheng Silk Store, Sent a Mr. Yu To The Bank At Night To Lure Me Away, Saying That If I Wanted To Prevent My Younger Brother From Being Sued, I Should Quickly Pay Off The Debt.

I Repaid Thousands of Yuan and Urged My Younger Brother to Behave Himself in The Future. However, Loyalty Is Hard to Hear. In the Last Quarter of Last Year, My Younger Brother Forged Zhuang Notes. He Was Reported and Punished By The Court. He Is Still In Prison. When the Case Occurred, I Hired a Lawyer to Defend My Younger Brother. The Expenses Were All Paid By Me. By The End of the Year, I Had Embezzled 40,000 Yuan From The Bank and 17,700 Taels of Silver. Although I Wanted to Make Amends,

I Had No Way to Do So.

I Had No Way Out But Suicide to Avoid Hurting the Guarantors and Damaging My Family's Reputation. So, On April 1, I Sneaked to Wusong and Wrote My Last Letter in a Hotel Room. I Coughed Up Several Mouthfuls of Blood at The Time. I Planned to Drown Myself in The Sea At Night. Because I Had Studied a Lot, I Tied a Lot of Books To My Body, Hoping That The Heavy Books Would Prevent The Body From Floating To The Surface After Entering The Sea. Late at Night, I Dissolved and Swallowed Two Bottles of Sleeping Pills. Then, I Walked Out of The Hotel. Unexpectedly, There Was an Iron Fence Outside The Hotel Door, Which I Could Not Cross. I Returned to The Room and Worshipped, Bidding Farewell to My Relatives and Friends. At This Time, The Medicine Had Taken Effect. I Do Not Know What Happened Afterwards Because I Was Unconscious. Now That I Am Alive Again, I Have No Other Request Than to Ask Judge and Chen Xuanzhen, Manager, to Specifically Forgive

Me For My Criminal Acts.

At This Point, He Collapsed, Unable to Speak. Judge Xu Waited For Him to Finish and Ordered Him to Open the Debate. The Police and the Bank's Lawyer Both Asked That He Be Punished According to Law, While Jiang Baolian Stated That the Defendant's Family and Guarantors Were Trying to Raise Funds to Repay the Money, Requesting Lenience. The Judge Then Ordered the Defendant to Be Taken Back to Prison and Set the Sentencing for Next Wednesday.

Chen Lao Jiu Died Really Bitterly 65

The Corpse Lay for Three Days and Nights Before Being Buried

After Burial, Thieves Stole the Coffin

Chen Lao Jiu (aka Jinfa), a farmer from the Zhang Family House Oil Mill at the East End of Shengjia Lane, Tangqiao, Pudong, because his newlywed wife, Hua, was used to certain habits and returned to her mother's house to live for two months. Chen repeatedly went to welcome her back to Ning, but his mother-in-law refused to let her go. Lao Jiu was angry and swallowed a piece of red arsenic in secret on the eleventh of this month, committing suicide. By 7:00 AM the next day, he died from the poison. Upon learning of this, the mother-in-law still did not send her daughter back to wear mourning clothes, but instead demanded compensation for dowry gold jewelry from the groom's family, which caused the Chen clan to be dissatisfied and go to question her. The bride had hidden the gold jewelry in the bag of a neighbor's daughter and it was discovered, causing a commotion and dispute. The details were reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that this case was mediated by friends and relatives from both sides, who blamed the Hua family for being wrong, ordering them to send their daughter back to the Chen family immediately to wear mourning clothes and observe her widowhood, thus settling the matter. The Chen family was poor, owing a lot of money since the engagement and marriage, with no savings. There was no money for the coffin and burial expenses. Therefore, the maternal family gave a discretionary subsidy. The corpse lay for three days and nights before being buried at 7:00 PM the day before yesterday (the fourteenth). That night, the corpse and coffin were carried to the field at the east end of the Zhang Family House for temporary burial. Unexpectedly, something unexpected happened. Chen's corpse coffin was pried open by thieves that night (commonly known as "upside-down fighting"), and all the burial clothes were stolen. Yesterday morning, a vegetable vendor noticed it on the way and the news spread, and the crowd of onlookers blocked the road. In the afternoon, the corpse's family brought Chen's old clothes to cover it, and the coffin lid was nailed on. The onlookers dispersed, saying that Chen Lao Jiu died really bitterly.

The Injured Male Corpse in Suzhou Creek 66

With a Giant Rock Weighing Dozens of Pounds on Its Back

Amazingly Able to Float, Truly an Unusual Phenomenon

Yesterday morning, a murdered male corpse floated up in the Suzhou Creek in front of the Yutong Flour Mill at Chedaijiao, Guangfu Road, North Gate. He was about twenty years old, wearing a yellow suit, an evergreen coat, white socks, and had a bald head. His hands and feet were tied with ropes, and there was a rope around his neck, with deep strangulation marks. His head was also stabbed in several places. Strangely, a giant rock weighing dozens of pounds was tied to his back, a situation commonly known as "planting lotus flowers." After killing the person, they were weighed down to the bottom of the river with a giant rock, surely ensuring that their bones and flesh would rot away and not be seen by anyone, so that the dead would become wronged souls without a chance to be redressed. This type of method is often found among boatmen who commit theft and evil deeds. However, it is truly an unusual phenomenon that this corpse, with a giant rock on its back, still floated up. At that time, after the Water Patrol Team rescued him, they sent Shen Xiaohe, the local security officer of the 27th Bao, 11th Tu, to

Page 12

Report the death to the District Court. Inspector Yang and others arrived at the scene to confirm that he was murdered and filled out an autopsy report. The Jia Charity Association was ordered to collect the body and await investigation of the family and arrest of the perpetrators.

Robbery at Zheng Jiansan's Home on Mongolia Road 67

Losses Amount to Nearly Four Thousand Yuan

Zheng Jiansan, a native of Zhenjiang, resides at No. 14, Rongshen Lane, Mongolia Road, Zhabei. He currently holds important positions at the Flying Star Rickshaw Company and the Tianchan Stage. His financial situation is prosperous, which has attracted the attention of bandits. At approximately 10:15 AM yesterday morning, Zheng and his wife were upstairs. Not long after getting up, after having breakfast, Zheng was planning to go out on business. The rickshaw puller and servants were chatting downstairs when they suddenly heard a knock on the door. The rickshaw puller went out to open the door and welcome the visitor in. The visitor reached into his pocket as if searching for something. The rickshaw puller initially thought he was taking out a business card, but suddenly the visitor pulled out a pistol and pointed it directly at his chest. Only then did he realize that it was a bandit. Six bandits quickly followed him in, four with pistols and two with Mauser pistols. One was wearing a blue lined spring jacket and pants, while the others were wearing long robes and copper basin hats. They entered the living room in single file, first inspecting the surroundings. One bandit guarded the telephone on the wall and asked if there was an alarm bell. Five bandits then went upstairs and broke into Zheng's bedroom. Zheng, seeing this, knew they were not good people. He intended to resist, but he did not have his own pistol with him that day. He was helpless. The bandits showed their weapons and demanded, "Behave yourself and hand over the keys!" Zheng, intimidated by their power, had no choice but to obey. After obtaining the keys, the bandits drove Zheng and his wife downstairs and locked them in the living room. The five bandits ransacked the cabinets and drawers, searching at will. After an hour, they left after their plunder. Zheng, seeing that the bandits had left, went upstairs to check the missing items. The stolen items included 1,400 yuan in cash, a diamond ring worth over 1,000 yuan, a pearl Ruyi and a string of pearls worth approximately 500-600 yuan, a gold wooden fish, a gold lock pendant, two pairs of gold buttons, two pairs of large and small gold bracelets, a satin lined coat, a black purple lambskin robe, a camel's wool robe, and a crepe cotton robe, totaling approximately 4,000 yuan. He filed a report with the relevant First Precinct of the Fourth District. Police Chief Dai immediately ordered the patrol captain to investigate the scene and instructed his subordinates to strictly arrest and prosecute the perpetrators.

At 10:15 PM last night, three bandits suddenly broke into No. 104 Shengan Road, Yangshupu. One of the bandits pulled out a pistol and threatened the victim, stealing only two hundred copper coins. The victim shouted loudly, and the patrol officers nearby arrived and arrested one person on the spot. He was immediately taken to the police station and will be sent to the court for review this morning.

Investigating the Impersonation of a Mail Truck to Transport Opium 69

According to the Continental Daily, since Sunday afternoon, French detectives seized a bag of opium from a car used by the post office at the Taikoo Wharf. The local postmaster has sent Qiu Weilai, a Westerner in charge of joint transportation of mail, to Beijing on the 13th to investigate the details of the Wusong ship. According to the postmaster, it is now found that the No. 14 mail truck did pass through the French Concession Pudong at that time, but there is no evidence to prove whether the truck was involved in the case. Qiu Weilai's investigation report concluded that the post office was not involved in the case because no witness was arrested, the owner of the car is unknown, and the bag containing the opium was not a post office bag. According to Deputy Inspector Li of the French Police Station, there is no evidence to prove that the car involved in the case was a post office vehicle. It is suspected that the car was impersonating a post office vehicle to avoid inspection by detectives.

Municipal Public Works Bureau 70

Bans Songyang Telephone Company From Raising Prices

The Wusong Songyang Telephone Company recently issued a notice stating that starting in April, the telephone fee for Type A users would be increased by half a yuan, and the telephone fee for Type B and C users would be increased by one yuan. Upon receiving the report, the Municipal Public Works Bureau stated that according to the Regulations on the Supervision of Private Public Utilities, the establishment or amendment of public utility fee collection methods related to public users should be reported to the supervisory authority for approval and record. The company increased the telephone fees for users without approval, which is inappropriate. It is said that the company has been ordered to publish an announcement and notify the cancellation of the fee increase.

Yesterday, Nanyang China on Longhua Road invited Master Taixu to lecture on Buddhism. The topic was "Buddhism and New Thought." He compared Russell's New Realism, Einstein's Theory of Relativity, and the latest Atomic Theory with Buddhism, stating that although there were many similarities, the subtlety, depth, and shallowness were vastly different. He also mentioned that vegetarianism and abstaining from killing animals are very popular in Europe and the United States. He witnessed this situation during his travels and examined the reasons. One reason is that meat contains toxins, which are harmful to hygiene. Another reason is that animals eating animals goes against humanity. Westerners deduce it from reason, believing that humans evolved from beasts, so the habit of eating meat has been passed down to this day and not forgotten. There were seven or eight hundred listeners that day, applauding and welcoming him enthusiastically.

Adultery Film Lawsuit Verdict 77

Both Ren and Chen are Sentenced to Fines

Original Bail Maintained During Appeal Period

Regarding the "Silent Love" film, Wu Airong’s stepmother, Madam Wu Yang, and her brother Wu Baolun, believed the film insulted their character. They filed a private lawsuit in the District Court against Ren Xifan, manager of the Xifan Film Company, director Chen Zhuomin, cinematographer Zhang Fukang, and Liang Zhongfen of the Current Affairs Film Company, accusing them of insult and defamation. The Criminal Division of the District Court conducted multiple investigations and summoned Lin Jim and Wu Airong, the original subjects of the film, for questioning. The plaintiff further requested an additional civil lawsuit for 3,000 taels in damages to reputation. After deliberation, the court found that the actions in the film, done without the permission of the individuals involved, inevitably defamed the reputation of others. Therefore, yesterday, Judge Qian Chengjun opened the court and declared Ren Xifan guilty of defamation and fined him 400 yuan, Chen Zhuomin guilty of defamation and fined him 200 yuan. Zhang Fukang was found not guilty, and Liang Zhongfen's trial was suspended. The civil lawsuit was transferred to the Civil Division. The defendants declared their dissatisfaction, and the court ordered that the original bail be maintained during the appeal period. Consequently, the defendants were released on bail by their guarantors.
