News from Trade Associations 80

The Brick and Ash Industry Trade Association held its first general membership meeting yesterday, chaired by Hu Qingchen. After reporting on the association's affairs, the following cases were discussed: (1) A letter from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce soliciting donations for disaster relief in Shaanxi Province. It was resolved to allocate the remaining funds from the association's welfare fund for this purpose, and that all fellow tradesmen should make every effort to donate, so as to gather strength from many sources. (2) The procedures for the Municipal Market's preparation are not yet complete, and how should it proceed? It was resolved that since the procedures for the Municipal Market's preparation are not yet complete, its establishment should be temporarily postponed. (3) A letter from the Coal Ash Factory regarding the price increase of coal ash. It was resolved that coal kiln operators are using the excuse of a shortage of Kailuan coal dust to drastically increase the market price of coal ash to five jiao per dan, which calculates to 2.35 yuan per load. According to all calculation methods and proportions, the increase should not be so large, which is clearly monopolistic speculation seeking exorbitant profits, disregarding our industry and indirectly bringing the construction industry of the entire city of Shanghai to a virtual standstill, which is extremely abhorrent. This association should send a letter uniformly rejecting this, and find ways to seek our own relief. At this point, Representative Zhu of the Municipal Party Headquarters said that freedom of business is enshrined in the Three Principles of the People. If the other party is taking the opportunity to speculate, we can obtain supplies directly from the production area. If obstacles arise, the law will provide protection. The attending representatives unanimously agreed to raise funds to establish an office for purchasing coal ash and implementing transportation and sales. Thirteen specialized committee members were immediately elected to purchase coal ash: Hu Qingya, Chen Jichang, Zhu Hongqi, Ling Shumei, Gu Hongxiang, Jia Shaoyan, Xu Menghua, Gong Binsheng, Zhou Gui, Zhang Songxian, Li Weixin, Wu Hongchang, and Wu Mengsheng, etc. The coal ash purchasing office was established within the association on the same day. (4) The issue of contracts between fellow tradesmen and ash kilns. It was resolved that since coal ash prices have skyrocketed and negotiations are already underway, it should be discussed after the coal ash issue is resolved. There is no question of signing contracts at present. (5) Member Sheng Xingpanhua reported that the self-transport of coal ash was unreasonably detained, requesting protection. It was resolved that it should be unanimously approved and protected. (6) The location of this association's headquarters is remote and not very suitable. Should a branch office be established in the concession? It was resolved to agree and establish a branch office at No. 275 Huile Lane, Yunnan Road, in the Public Concession. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

The Shanghai eyewear industry giants, Zhuang Honggao, Dong Zixing, Zhang Shide, Wang Shuoquan, Wang Wende, Yin Zaiqing, Yu Zhimin, Chu Zimin, Bao Ziyuan, Yan Kanghou, Fan Jiating, Xue Hesun, Li Chaifeng, Wu Zhusun, Jia Songting, etc., previously believed that the old Chinese Eyewear Association's organization was not in accordance with the law. They specially presented a request to the Municipal Party Headquarters for permission to reorganize it into the Shanghai Municipal Eyewear Industry Trade Association to comply with the law. However, some members of the trade do not understand the truth of the reorganization and are still observing and hesitating to join. It is reported that the association issued a letter to those who have not yet joined. A excerpt is as follows: "To our esteemed colleagues: The way of doing business values competition, but even more so, unity. If there is only competition without unity, it will inevitably lead to failure. This is why all industries have trade associations. On the government side, it is hoped that all industries and businesses have sufficient unity to revitalize commerce and recover rights and interests. The Law on Industrial and Commercial Trade Associations was specially promulgated to bring businessmen into the correct path, aiming for the prosperity of commerce. It also stipulates that each industry association has the qualifications of members in the General Chamber of Commerce, and has the right to make suggestions and supervise. In law, it is a legal group, with the right to elect and be elected. The legislation is perfect, and the plan is thorough. However, at this time of initiating business tax, official procedures are cumbersome, and the burden on businessmen increases. The Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce advocates that matters relating to business tax be handled by the Chamber of Commerce, and has petitioned the Ministry of Finance. It is bound to be implemented. The Shanghai Municipal Business Tax has also been proposed by the Tax Rules Research Association to be first recognized by the authorities by each industry association, and then apportioned according to the actual business situation. Matters are made public, and the tax is only minimal, avoiding the official form of harassment and reducing the invisible burden on businessmen. It is found that each industry in Shanghai has a strict organization, but our eyewear industry is very scattered. At this time of close and vital interests, without sufficient unity, not only will the loss in business tax be very large, but it will also decline from now on, and be scorned by various industries. This association is deeply concerned about this. We convened a meeting to discuss and unanimously decided to notify the colleagues to join the association quickly and unite our strength. Do not give up the inherent rights and legal protection. If there are any difficult incidents, this association has hired a year-round legal advisor, who will not find it difficult to resolve them. It is also planned to set up an Optometry Research Association in this association, hiring specialized knowledge, specializing in research, and striving to promote our industry, so that it will develop more and more, and receive the effect of a thousand benefits without a single disadvantage. Certificates will also be printed and filled out at any time to serve as a pledge of faith. We specially send this letter to you and ask your company to join immediately and jointly promote the progress. The future of the association is deeply reliant on it. A membership application form is attached, please fill it out and reply. I wish you good fortune."

World Snippets 82

— Hai Ke

▲Bavaria, one of the German states. Since the European War, it has faced economic difficulties. In one large hotel, the tablecloths and napkins used were entirely made of paper. Others used oats instead of coffee, breadcrumbs instead of rice. Butter was also not obtained from cows, but artificially made.

▲In British hospitals, no less than several thousand frogs are needed each year for scientific dissection. Before the war, many people made a living from this. However, in recent years, no one is willing to do this frog-catching life anymore.

▲Phototelegraphy has already been successfully tested in France. Using their method, the sender's own handwriting can be sent to the person receiving the telegram. It is even more reliable when important matters are involved.

▲The British merchant ship "Lusitania" was sunk by a German submarine in 1915. Five million gold pounds in cash sank to the bottom of the sea. The British government tried to salvage it.

▲Hayes, England, has government warehouses that store many public goods. There was an auction. Two aviators bought two old airplanes for two pounds and ten shillings. For the engine alone, each plane was worth fifty pounds.

Anecdotes of Mr. Fu Junjian 83

— Fang Er

My friend Mr. Fu Junjian suddenly passed away. Many people in Hunan mourned him. After welcoming his coffin back, the government held a public memorial service and requested a commendation from the provincial government, in consideration of the death of the old poet Zeng Chongbo, who lived in splendor but died in desolation. It is truly another wave of emotion. Here are one or two things written to express my lingering sadness and sighing for the past.

Mr. Fu's courtesy name was Tun Gen, from Liling. He was born with intelligence and was considered a child prodigy. He was skilled in poetry and prose, not conforming to vulgar tunes, and good at finger calligraphy, strong and vigorous, not casually written, not easily obtained. In the thirteenth year of the Republic, I worked with him in a certain school. One day, he recited a quatrain to me, saying, "I have not seen Tan San for half a year, his fame and fortune are known to be in the ascendant. How about a short flute across the back of a cow, quiet valleys and clear streams are enough to sleep." Asked what he thought of the poem, I thought Mr. Fu's poem was great and praised it greatly. He said that one must have joy with Tan Gong like Mr. Fu to write the words Tan San, and one must be as noble as Mr. Fu to have the words quiet valleys and clear streams. Mr. Fu said, "This was written by a new noble in our village before he came out of the mountains." Everyone thinks it is my poem when I recite it to others, so we laughed together for a long time.

Another day after class, my colleagues and I were chatting in the lounge. Mr. Fu suddenly arrived, laughing and shouting, "I've been burned by fire, I've been burned by fire!" Everyone was startled and asked about the situation. Then he smiled and said, "The wildfire burned me, it doesn't matter." He took out a roll of newspapers from his bag. Everyone looked at it. It was the Wildfire supplement of the Xiang Bao, written by Mr. Wang Fuquan and Zhang Tiemin. The purpose was to advocate vernacular literature and attack classical literature. The target was Mr. Fu as a poet of the Southern Society and a classical writer, and Mr. Wu Fangji as a eight-legged essay teacher. (Wu was also working at a certain school at that time) The spears were aimed at him from all sides, strong and unparalleled. Mr. Fu said that there is no such thing as literary language in literature, the key is to seek truth. I have always held this view, but they only attack me with poetry and classical writing, regarding me as stubborn and old-fashioned, which is not accurate. However, the friends in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River (as the Wildfire people called themselves) are known to be slippery, daring to fight hard with the barbarians of Hunan, not afraid of getting burned, their courage is also great. After speaking, he laughed loudly, and everyone laughed. Later, government officials suspected that Wildfire had incited student unrest, and hinted that the Xiang Bao should stop publishing. The Wildfire people thought it was at Mr. Fu's instruction, but they did not see Mr. Fu's breadth of mind.

Witty Remarks 84

— Fei Wenbao

My teacher, Mr. Fan Jingmei, has been known in the business world for many years for his diligent and capable work. Mr. Fan was busy with work until last spring, at the age of forty-three, when he held his wedding ceremony. Knowing good things were coming to his door, many wished him to have a son soon. This spring, he did indeed have a son. When holding the birth celebration, relatives and friends congratulated Mr. Fan on obtaining this beautiful son in the shortest period of time, which shows that no matter what he does, he has a considerable grasp of it. Everyone raised their glasses to congratulate him. Mr. Fan smiled and said that he "stumbled upon" it. There was no so-called certainty. Everyone laughed loudly. According to the Shanghai dialect, "stumbling upon" means accidental. (Received payment)

Writing About the Expedient Actions of a Wise Mother 85

Z> Bingxin

Between Jiangsu and Zhejiang, there is a large town. The population is dense, and the commerce is prosperous. At the turn of February and March of this year, the newly prevalent meningitis epidemic spread to the town, extending to the surrounding villages. The villagers and townspeople usually have god-welcoming celebrations in the spring. Later, due to the government's decrees of the Republic to eliminate superstition, the authorities strictly banned it, and this custom was slightly reduced. This year, the people were again bewitched by the saying that the plague god could ward off the plague. They raised funds and scheduled to parade the plague god through the town. The sub-district chief of the local public security bureau of the township heard the news and immediately issued a notice, clarifying the ban and earnestly advising that there were good methods for epidemic prevention, and that clay figures had no power to remedy. However, the ignorant people were obsessed and did not realize the truth, and the progress became more vigorous. The sub-district chief, with the meeting date approaching, was deeply concerned that it would be a waste of people and money, and easily cause trouble, so he took urgent measures to carry the plague god idol to the sub-district office, lock it in an empty room, and apply to the superior official to send police to supervise and suppress it. However, the people gathered men, women, old and young three days before the meeting date, each holding incense, surrounding the sub-district office, shouting and petitioning, declaring that if they could not get it back, they would burn the sub-district office or forcibly seize the idol. At the time of the event, the situation was turbulent. The armed police sent by the superior numbered only four, combined with the local sub-district police, their number was less than two percent of the population. The sub-district chief was about to send the police to break through and rush to ask the superior official to send additional police to coordinate the suppression when his mother heard about it and scolded, "The situation is urgent! You want to make this place follow in the footsteps of Dongyang County!" Moreover, the people's crime is only superstition, and it is not to the point of death. Are you going to treat them like whales and sharks? And there is no reason to send troops to suppress them. The sub-district chief said, "That's true. But violating the decree will likely lead to dismissal." The mother said, "Haha! If the villages and towns are ruined, can you alone protect yourself?" "Then what should I do?" The mother said, "Return the idol, warn them not to cause trouble, and send police to accompany the meeting on the meeting date for strict protection, then the people will be happy. If the epidemic does not stop afterward, the people will be disappointed and realize the truth. Even if it doesn't, you can avoid burning everything. Do it quickly! You can't delay it for a moment!" The sub-district chief obeyed. The crowd was appeased. On the day of welcoming the god, the sub-district police armed with protection were fortunate that nothing happened. Afterward, the superior officials appreciated his feelings and did not blame him. The sub-district chief was very happy and thanked his mother. The mother said, "You can go. The government is not smooth, and the people are not harmonious. A pro-people official is beyond your capabilities." The sub-district chief resigned and left with his mother. How wise is the mother! To call it expedient and adaptable, who says it is not appropriate. As for the so-called plague god, with a mud body and a porcelain head, it is said that two hundred years ago, a kiln owner burned a kiln for seven days and seven nights. When the kiln was opened, there was nothing but a porcelain head, like the plague god's shape. So he assembled a mud body and served it carefully. Is it a fact? Is it a fabrication? It is unknowable and unnecessary to study. The names of the sub-district chief and his mother were not mentioned by the informer, so I omit them.

Recording Min Cuiying's Sitting in the Palace 86

— Tian Wen

Ms. Min Cuiying is the daughter of Mr. Xin Wu, a large merchant from eastern Zhejiang. She was educated at home from an early age and is naturally intelligent. She has a foundation in both Chinese and Western languages and is passionate about art. She learned charcoal painting. In just a few days, she could achieve a lifelike resemblance. Her extraordinary intelligence is like this. She is particularly interested in Peking opera. She learned the female roles, but without a particular school. She can gather the strengths of each school to form her own style. She has a strong desire to reform Peking opera. She once performed a revised version of "Su San's Release" with Shanghai people at the New Oriental Theater. She became famous at once and had the reputation of an artist. Yesterday, she was invited by the Pingshe amateur troupe to perform "Visiting Mother in the Palace" at the Ningbo Native Place Association. Ms. Min left behind the Iron Mirror Princess, looking beautiful. The dignified and graceful were expressed in the beautiful and elegant. At the entrance, the opening line of the Yao board "The sun is shining, the spring is beautiful, and the birds are singing" requires a small tune. The ultimate effect is extremely euphemistic and roundabout. The three "He He Shi Le" in the slow board are accompanied by different facial expressions. She can express the thoughts of a woman's family. A person without wisdom will never understand this. The entire slow board song is like jade, round and smooth. The pace is moderate. The highlights in the allegro are repeatedly seen. Especially the two lines "Thinking of home, thinking of flesh and blood, I can't be reunited" and "What heartfelt things do you want to say in detail" are appropriately modulated. The most moving. As for the clarity of the Beijing dialect and the formal style of the figure, they are secondary matters.

Ten Thousand People Block the Road to Keep the County Magistrate 87

— Xia Hu

Lu Zongfu, the county magistrate of Jincheng County, Shanxi Province, whose courtesy name is Boxiong, is a graduate of Peking University and has a close relationship with me. Lu's wife is the younger sister of Ye Yuhu, a virtuous internal assistant. He first served as an official in Jiang County, Shanxi, etc., and was transferred to Jincheng not long ago. He has a good reputation wherever he goes. His father, Mr. Tijun, is a well-known filial and incorrupt official, with the title of "Good Old Man." His younger brother, Mengsheng, graduated from Jiaotong University and specializes in electrical engineering. He recently served as the director of a wireless station in Shanghai. Last year, when Yan Feng rebelled, the Shanxi army frequently requisitioned, and Jincheng was right in the middle of it. Fortunately, Magistrate Lu took appropriate measures, and the place was safe. Therefore, the people greatly appreciated him. At the beginning of February of this year, Shanghai newspapers suddenly published the news that the county magistrate of Jincheng had been shot and killed by Sun Dianying's troops. Lu's old father was uneasy after reading the newspaper. It happened to be New Year's Eve according to the old calendar, and the whole family was gloomy. After a telegram from the Shanxi County Government, the truth was revealed. My friend Zhu Qingyuan, a classmate of Lu, in order to comfort Lu's relatives and friends, published an article in the Aixkees Optical three-day journal that he runs, which was extremely detailed. Lu's parents, thinking of their son being a petty official thousands of miles away, repeatedly telegraphed him to return. Lu also had the thoughts of a wanderer missing his parents and resolutely resigned, but as soon as his resignation was submitted, the people of Jincheng actually blocked the road and cried to keep him. Only after Lu agreed to withdraw his resignation did they cheer and disperse. "A good official is still a scholar." Magistrate Lu can be worthy of it. My ancestor, Lan Gao, was an official in Boluo County, Guangdong, and also had political achievements. On the day of his departure, the villagers all sent him off with tears. To this day, there is still a monument to my ancestor's departure in Boluo. Since the Republic of China, Wang Renpu and Fei Zuoquan, two county magistrates of our salt county, also had the benevolence of Gan Tang and Shao Fu. Wang was meritorious in treating rice borers, and the villagers still praised him. Wang was good at calligraphy and painting, and his other name was Chun Daoren. Therefore, I also write it down to encourage those who are now local officials.

However, they must pay postage, which is 5 jiao and 2 fen for the whole year and 2 jiao and 6 fen for half a year, and provide relevant proof to prevent fraud. (Red)

India Travelogue (25) 89

— Ling Hua

Gandhi was born in Rajkot, a place in West India. Rajkot is not far from Mumbai. Gandhi's father was over forty years old when he was born. At the age of seven, according to Indian custom, he married. He was timid by nature, afraid of thieves, snakes, and ghosts. His courage was far less than his wife's. Indian religions prohibit eating meat. As a child, he learned to smoke, stealing money from servants to buy cigarettes. Later, he resolved to repent. He ate meat several times within a year when he was a teenager. Later, he swore to his mother to abstain completely. After the age of eighteen, he studied in England. Their clan system did not allow going abroad, because going to foreign countries required eating with foreigners. The elders expelled him from the church. This shows how important Indians considered eating together. He studied law in England for three years. He traveled to Paris and visited the Exposition and the highest Eiffel Tower. He quoted Tolstoy's mocking words about the Eiffel Tower: "This thing cannot represent the architect's wisdom, but only his stupidity, because it will soon oppress people's spirits under the tower." This was his criticism against materialism. He followed Tolstoy, and was even more courageous. Tolstoy also said, "We are not children now, we can be fooled by this toy." After returning to China, he worked as a lawyer in Mumbai in 1893. Later, he went to South Africa, because Indians were not allowed to sit in second-class carriages there and were beaten by white people for no reason. This aroused the idea of ​​national self-determination. He bought a first-class ticket, but was not allowed to ride in the first-class carriage. When he went to the shops where Indians were, the white people took them away and did not eat with them. There were even so-called special laws in Transwaal, a British territory. In Transwaal, Indians were not allowed to walk on public roads and were not allowed to travel after 9 p.m. All kinds of mistreatment led him to guide the masses and launch a movement for autonomy, starting with the Indian overseas Chinese in South Africa. After three years in South Africa, he returned to Mumbai and the movement was very effective. He failed in Calcutta, so he took his family back to South Africa. He was often beaten by white people. He was spared thanks to the protection of a police officer's wife. When he returned home from South Africa for the second time, the overseas Chinese gave him a lot of gold, silver, and diamonds. He gave them all away, saying, "These are superfluous things." In 1901, he returned to India and visited the Deer Park and various Indian temples. He always took third-class carriages. After going to various places to hold meetings and promote autonomy, he went to South Africa again. He promoted the use of local products by the local people, with each family doing their own labor, weaving cloth for their own use. Gandhi himself did the laundry and could cut his own hair. He was very effective. He relied on the power of the Indian religion. He devoted himself to proving the effectiveness of vegetarianism with science. He did not advocate class struggle, but used persuasion. This autobiography only ends with the first volume. There is still a second volume, which I heard has just been published. The whole volume is written in a self-narrating tone, which can be compared with Sun Yat-sen's autobiography and Kropotkin's autobiography. I read a magazine in my early years that said his father was a high official, and compared this autobiography to it. That was a mistake in translation and hearsay. There are many powerful Indian poems in his book. The motto is "Do my duty, even if I fail, I will be honored." Many of his poems are in the book Gita, which has an English translation.

The Gold Market Outlook is Peaceful

Early swap market offered by bulls. Yesterday, the benchmark gold price on the 15th fell and then rose again. The market trend remained flat. There were only two or three lots of trades. However, a total of ten lots were reviewed throughout the day, and eventually rose slightly by two taels. Since the swap period had arrived, the transactions of each bank were not significant, and the market became sluggish early in the morning. Stimulated by the rebound in the silver market, there were still more sellers afterwards, once breaking the 710 tael level. However, the exchange rate was extremely peaceful and the listing price remained the same. It seemed to be improving in the future, because buyers were diligent. The market was usually weak on Wednesdays due to the exchange rates, so it was still calm at the beginning. It was said that each bank had started doing swap business in advance. The bulls still offered, initially at 2.50 taels, but then the bulls, believing that their cash reserves were not large, were unwilling to offer too much, so the bears could not force the price up. The price was then reduced to 2 taels, and then a little over 2 taels. Each bank, such as Shunli, Wanxing, Hengxing, Tong Taichang, Zhenchang, and Xiang, had swap transactions with each other, and quite a few people traded based on today's listed price. It was also found that firms such as Yuancheng, Xinheng, Yongheng, and spot traders were short, while Wanxing, Shunli, Yuanheng, Fuchang, and Wu were long. There were not many transactions in May, but suddenly large firms such as Chenfeng and Yong began to compete for purchases, which led to a strong upward trend, from soft to sharp. This was due to speculation. The closing price was the highest, reaching more than 718 taels. There may be no changes in the big bars this morning, but the gold price can be expected to improve.

Morning opening fell slightly by 6.50 taels. The opening price for May this morning fell slightly by 6.50 taels, to 710 taels. The big bars rebounded by one-eighth, the silver price increased by one-quarter, and private telegrams also increased by five-sixteenths. Afterwards, Yuanxing Yong Shunli Wanxing and others entered the market, increasing by three taels, to 12.50 taels. However, Hengxing Yuan and some speculators sold, and the price immediately fell, to only 0.85 taels. When the exchange rate was announced, there were fluctuations of more than two taels, from 11 taels to 0.9 taels. There were no changes in the listing price. The domestic market was still stable. British gold was absorbed by the bank at 13.50, and Zhongfu sold to Holan at the same price in May. The arbitrageurs, Fuchang, Richang, and Hengxing, all bought in, so the price increased by three taels, to 12.50 taels at 9:50. After 10:00, Hengxing Yuan, Qianchang, Xiang Yuanmao Yong, and others tended to sell, and the price was reduced by three taels. There was still some hedging. The exchange rate remained unchanged. Mitsui once offered Japanese gold for May at 11.575 taels. Around 11:00, it fell to 0.9 taels. Afterwards, British gold for July was in demand by Mitsui and others at 13.50, and there were many buyers on the floor. At 11:45, it rebounded to 12.50 taels, and then fluctuated by one tael. It once reached 11.50 taels, and the closing price was 12 taels. The announced price was still 777 taels, from 67.80 taels to 64.50 taels.

The afternoon trend gradually increased slightly. The afternoon opening price was 12.80 taels, followed by 2.90 taels. There were many buyers. Suddenly, news of an increase in the Indian exchange rate of 2 annas suppressed the price to 11.67 taels. Zhifeng Yong and others bought in, and the price rose to 13.50 taels. Subsequently, Yu Da and others sold, and the price fell by more than one tael. However, trading was brisk, because the swap market had already opened privately in the market. The price fell to 12 taels until 3:30. Afterwards, it seemed to show a sharp upward trend, because large firms such as Chenfeng, Yong, Daxing, Yongyi, and Fengyong suddenly started buying, and the market soared. After 4:00, it had exceeded 17 taels, with only one tael of fluctuation. The closing price at 4:30 reached 18.30 taels, an increase of 1.80 taels compared to the previous day. The price had already been done to 8.50 taels. The price of goods decreased by 0.03 taels. The maximum price for the day was 18.30 taels, and the minimum price was 0.85 taels (based on the listed price), a difference of 9.80 taels. The morning price of goods was 11.50 taels, and the afternoon closing price was 11.50 taels. The afternoon price was 12 taels, and the closing price was 18 taels. The announced price decreased by 65 taels to 59 taels. The registered price was 12 taels in the morning and 18 taels in the afternoon. The make-up water was 0.08 taels in the afternoon and 14 taels.

There were no large transactions among the firms. The firms that sold were Tong Taichang, Tian Fengyong, Juchang, Hongli, Yongfeng, Yu Da, Cuichang Yong, Yuanmao Yong, etc. The firms that bought were Zhifeng Yong, Yuancheng Yong, Wanxing, Shunli, Fuchang, Yuanheng, and Hengxing. Art World

A Visit to the Morning Light Art Society 101

— Huang Jun

The Fifth Exhibition is About to Open

In the springtime, with the sound of birds chirping, the sky is boundless blue, and the wildflowers are in full bloom. Looking into the distance at the powder-green forest, interspersed with a few eye-catching red flowers, clinging to the foot of the spring mountain like ink, a few houses, a few barks of dogs. At this moment, walking on Jiangwan Road, I felt as if I were intoxicated by the mellow wine brewed in spring. The weather was exceptionally warm, and occasionally a spring breeze gently caressed the lush green branches. Being confined for a few months in a house where I could not see a single bit of the clear sky, like a monk in an ancient temple, I was fortunate enough to experience a bit of nature's flavor this time. Although I walked alone, my heart was filled with boundless joy, no less than that of a lark soaring in the sky. When I walked to Garden Street, the surroundings were completely shaded by tree branches. Suddenly, a cool air passed through my entire body. The quiet beauty of spring's eternal painting made me take lighter steps, not daring to make any rude sounds, lest I wake the spring god who was guarding this place from his midday nap. Apart from me leisurely walking by, there were only a few swallows flying low to the ground.

I saw a building with a Western ancient flavor, standing out from the surrounding greenery. I knew this

was the Morning Light Art Society.

So, my walk made a temporary stop here.

I knocked on their door, which was not closed, and a waiter immediately led me into their room, which was upstairs facing the street. It had the advantage of enjoying the morning sun and evening glow, without the noise of traffic. This was truly a great place to paint.

At this time, Mr. Wang was in front of an easel, raising his sharp and spirited eyes to look at me, and greeted me in this way:

"Ah, I haven't seen you for a long time..."

"Mr. Wang, you are really busy."

I found that the corner of the wall was piled with oil paintings, and the paintbrushes in their hands still seemed very busy. Three or four people were painting non-stop.

"Because we have a scheduled exhibition date! April 25th! Very close to now."

"I think most of it is finished."

"Those are all painted. There are still a few that have not been completed."

"Mr., I think this exhibition will definitely be more satisfying for everyone."

"Not necessarily," he was still mixing colors on the palette, but a restless smile appeared on his face.

"Which session is this?"

"The fifth session."

"Ah, it has a long history."

"Our first exhibition, if I remember correctly, was in 1920."

"Because of the long period of time, your output must be very large now."

So, I walked to the place where the painting boards were stacked and flipped through them casually.

"Are there any other subjects here?"

"Yes, our output not only includes revolutionary history but also many Chinese ancient legends, as well as descriptions of the current suffering of the people."

"I think these are very important to us."

There were several easels placed in the room, and everyone was looking at the painting from different angles. Mr. Wang was concentrating all his energy on the painting. In the moment of stopping the brush, he sometimes scratched his hair in bitter contemplation, and sometimes showed a gentle smile. I saw the difficulty of creation here. But these many works stacked on the four walls, I don't know how much time and energy they took. At this time, I felt the greatness of the artists even more, creating a mythic world of beauty for us.

Not daring to disturb their work with endless talk, I just looked at the many works on my own, but the mood in my heart changed with the different tunes.

I saw a work titled "Red Terror," which gave me a great shock. It was a person with a blue face and fangs, holding a sharp blade in his hand, jumping out of the flames. This person was very much like a demon in mythology. The second was "Impression of Changsha," which almost awakened the terror of being frightened several times a night in my hometown. Countless naked men and women were lying on the ground, still bleeding. The dark smoke of the dim sky and the wind swirled, and the red tongues of fire rushed over. The cries of the people struggling and moaning under the massacre were still faintly discernible. So, I immediately retreated to my original seat, breathing abnormally fast, as if I were possessed by a nightmare. However, they were all still working there, taking a short break for a few minutes before I gradually woke up from the chaotic thoughts. So, I flipped through it again. In that stack of works, the work titled "Creation" used dim tones everywhere to bring out the gradually bright mountain top. If I guessed correctly, the person stretching out his arms might be because, in the sound sleep of the night, a flash of lightning suddenly flashed across the sky, like the dazzling light in the painting, shaking open the mountains and forests, and waking up the sleeping person. So, in the moment of jumping up, the sun spewed out ten thousand golden snakes in the mountains that were towering into the clouds, giving the world light and heat again. At this time, I also seemed like the person who stretched out his arms and shouted to the sky.

Many other powerful and vivid good works all jumped into my eyes. There were also a few titled "Virgin Killing the Snake," "Nüwa," and "Houyi Shooting the Sun," all descriptions of ancient legends. I broke the silence with a surprised voice, and Mr. Wang, moved by my curiosity, immediately put down his paintbrush and turned to explain the meaning of each picture to me. I stood beside him listening, as interesting as when I was a child listening to adults telling me stories.

Mr. Wang saw my childish smile, and he smiled too.

The last rays of the sun shone into the window, and my eyes shifted to the works depicting war. Seeing the revolutionary soldiers crossing the Yellow River, seeing thousands of people gathering there to hold a mass meeting, and the observation on the battlefield, all made me feel the enthusiasm and madness. So, in the midst of the ever-changing situation, I felt as if I had enjoyed a grand feast. Although I had seen several art exhibitions before, the impressions they gave me all disappeared like faint smoke long ago, and there was not a single one that made me linger. Although I am not worthy of mentioning art and appreciation, the impression I got today will never be forgotten. So, I expressed my thanks to Mr. Wang in this way:

"Today, it is the first time I have come into contact with works surrounded by a life aura."

"No, we still feel that these small gains are not enough."

"Well said... well said..."

When I lit a cigarette and looked at the approaching twilight outside, everyone had stopped writing and was preparing to go back in a hurry.

So, I shook hands with Mr. Wang and hurried out of the Morning Light Art Society, my heart still filled with longing at this moment.

Ah, artists are the supreme creators.

Art World Submission Guidelines 102

(1) Articles should be limited to news, reviews, and introductions about the latest art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature, both domestic and foreign.

(2) Photos should be limited to recent portraits and works by domestic and foreign artists, as well as various photographs related to the characters.

(3) The number of words in each article should not exceed 2,000.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(5) Write horizontally, do not write carelessly. Western characters can be omitted if possible. If you have to quote the original text, you must attach it below the translation.

Youth Corner

Random Notes on a Trip North 103

— Anping

IX. My Grandmother

As soon as the train passed Jinan, it gradually got dark. That night, I went to sleep very early because I had to change trains in Tianjin early the next morning to go to Beiping. I slept very well that night. However, for some reason, I seemed to see my grandmother. Needless to say, that was just a dream. I have to admit that I did dream of my grandmother that night. Although I no longer remember the details of that dream, I must say that my grandmother was one of the people in the world who loved me the most, and one of the people in the world who had the greatest kindness to me. I, who lost my mother six days after being born, was entirely raised by my grandmother. The spiritual comfort and pleasure I gave my grandmother is another matter. My grandmother raised me, loved me, and educated me. At least I have to admit that without her, there would not be a me who is still acceptable today. She could never forget her little grandson in everything. She would give Anping candy first, cut a piece of nice fabric for Anping first, and take Anping with her wherever she went to play. In all my memories, she never hit me more than five times. It is natural to say that an adult not hitting a child is not love, but she could not bear to hit me. She loved me, but I cannot say that she spoiled me. Troubles come from chopsticks, and filial sons come from pampering. She also said that her way of teaching me, the most effective method was not hitting, but the "expression" on her face. She usually loved me so much, but when she put on a stern look, everyone was afraid. She always said that Anping was unlucky and looked at my fair face. What did I know when I was little?

I had never left my grandmother until the year I first went to Nanjing to study. It was only then that I understood my grandmother's love.

Things in the world are often like this. You have to wait until you know this is happiness before you are no longer happy. Who doesn't think childhood is lovely, but who feels that childhood is lovely during childhood? Likewise, I said that I only really understood my grandmother's love then, but from that year on, I could no longer get my grandmother's love. My grandmother died in May of that year. Died.

I really don't want to think about these things anymore because thinking about these things will make me sad. What I relied on when I was little was my grandmother, and what my grandmother only got pleasure from was me. For the sake of her grandson's studies, she helped him pack his bedding and luggage with great pleasure. However, after my grandmother died, what did the family members talk about when they reminisced? They said that after I went to Nanjing, my grandmother's life underwent a very dark change. Her life seemed to have lost a lively sun and often became very gloomy and melancholy. Every time she received a letter from me from school in Nanjing, she was happy as if she had something. She called people to read it to her, once, twice, three times. Because my grandmother was seriously ill, I rushed back from Nanjing. My family was also happy, saying that her most beloved grandson had rushed back and that it might make her feel better. As soon as I ran home, I buried my head in her arms. God, what did I know then? She no longer had the strength to say a word, and I didn't know what was the most appropriate thing to say to comfort her. I just lay on the edge of the bed like a little lamb, letting her touch my bare little face. She closed her eyes, focused her spirit, as if touching a rare treasure, and occasionally lifted her eyelids to look at me, to see if I was thin or fat.

God no longer stayed her for another year or half for the misfortune of her little grandson. She died in May of that year.

After my grandmother died, I never had anyone who loved me like my grandmother loved me. My grandmother died ten years ago. I often remember her, but I rarely dream of her, rarely dreaming of her once in a year or two. But if I really dream of her, it seems that this dream has some meaning.

The one who loved me the most was my grandmother, and the one my grandmother loved the most was me. Even after she died, her soul still often patrolled around me. Whenever something very unusual happened, I would dream of her. That time in the car, I dreamed of my grandmother again. After waking up from the dream, I missed her strangely and was also strangely grateful to her. If there is such a thing as a soul, I believe that her soul is always patrolling and protecting me.

X. From Tianjin to Beiping

Before dawn on the fifth, the porter woke up all the guests. The train from Pukou to Beiping did not need to change trains in Tianjin, but during the few days I went to Beiping that time, it was said that it had to change. The porter woke up many guests so early, no more than to let everyone tidy up their personal belongings so that they could collect some "tips".

Tianjin has a total of three stations, one called the Old Station, one called the Main Station, and another I forgot the name of. I don't know which station I came down from. It was just dawning when I arrived in Tianjin. The distant electric lights were sparkling like the stars in the sky. People in the car really didn't feel cold. As soon as they got out of the car, the wind alone was enough to make people suffer.

After sitting in the waiting room for a while, they said that the train to Beiping had arrived, so I ran out again. Because I was not familiar with the road, I called a porter to carry my briefcase for me. Rather than saying he was carrying things, it was better to say that I called him to lead the way. From that car to this car, it was really just a few steps. He said there were rules and that he wanted four dimes from me. I thought the people in the north were honest, and anyway, I was coming to the north for the first time, so I didn't care and gave it to him. But when I got on the train to Beiping, I saw that people with six or seven pieces of luggage had not given two dimes. Only then did I realize that I had been cheated.

If I had gone to Beiping and only stayed for three or five days before returning, then Beiping, just the climate, would have given me a very bad impression. There is nothing to worry about in the north except for the wind. When it blows, there is nothing you can do. Just walking out of a car with a climate like the fourth or fifth month in Jiangnan, how could you stand it? People in the north mostly wear leather hats that can be turned down and leather coats with very high and wide collars. The use of these is all here. For example, in Shanghai, the collar of a leather coat is two inches wide, that's enough. In the north, it has to be twice as wide. I really suffered that day. When I was waiting for the train, it felt like there was wind everywhere, drilling straight into your neck. The ears gradually changed from soft to hard, and the nose was the same. Moreover, the snot slowly flowed out like a spring.

The second-class car on the Pingjin Road is simply not much different from the third class. It is equally old, broken, and untidy. It takes three hours to get from Tianjin to Beiping. The countryside in the north is always so monotonous. I remember when I returned to Jiangnan from Beiping, as soon as I stepped on the Jinghu Line, there was green grass, blue water, lovely. In the north, don't say on the train, but in any wilderness, I am afraid you can't find a beautiful scenery like Jiangnan. It is an endless expanse of thousands of acres of yellow soil, and you can't see where the sky and the earth meet. Or, those are some distant shadows of trees, a row of gray and black, often in mid-air, rising a streak of white air, cutting off the waist of the tree shadows. You would guess that this white air is clouds or fog, but I have to say it is sand.

The gray sand in the north is really powerful. When it comes, you close your eyes and feel small grains of sand sprinkling on your face. The north doesn't have rain often like Jiangnan, and the land is dry and loose all year round, so it flies up when it encounters wind.

The train arrived in Beiping around 11 o'clock in the morning. After getting off the train, I followed the others out of the platform, not knowing east from west. I wanted to find a hotel first. Before leaving Shanghai, someone said that the Garden Hotel and the Central Hotel were good. The Garden Hotel was just a little farther away, and the Central Hotel, if there was no bath room, would be fine for more than three dollars a room. I decided to look for the Central, but in the end, I never met the Central's receptionist. I just vaguely followed the Oriental Hotel's receptionist to the Oriental.

The Oriental Hotel's receptionist put me in a car and sent me from the station to the hotel. Although the people in the north are famously honest, for the sake of caution, I asked:

"Is this car specially prepared by your hotel to pick up guests?"

He said yes. I thought some hotels in Shanghai also had their own cars to pick up guests. I asked again:

"Then the fare is not borne by the guests, right?"

He also said yes. He said that the fare was calculated by the accounting room of their hotel. I thought that asking this, there would be no problems, so I sat in it.

From the station to the Oriental, hiring a rickshaw would probably not cost even a dime. With such a short distance, the car arrived in less than three or four minutes. Businessmen always love to make exorbitant demands. The waiter led me into a big room for twelve dollars a day. I laughed and said that I was not taking office as a committee member here, so why live in such a good room?

In the end, I lived in a room for three dollars a day, which was not bad. There was a radiator, but before I had even sat down, a signature slip was sent upstairs, saying that I had to sign it. I took a look, and it was the car fare just now, a big pan of one dollar and forty cents. The meaning was that after I signed it, I didn't have to pay now, and it would be calculated together when the room fee was calculated in the future. I knew I had been cheated, so I had to call the receptionist who picked me up from the station just now to come up and ask. He also knew he was wrong and just used some irrelevant words to beg for mercy in front of me. The waiters in Beiping are born with a cautious face and a humble attitude. I thought, forget it, anyway, I took the car myself, so pay it.

But because I was afraid that they would squeeze me again, it made me have to ask the price even when I called for a bowl of noodles later.

Establishing the Shanghai East Office of the Caoye Society 104

The Shanghai Caoye Society, located at 34 Fairen Road, was established on April 15th, 1929. The inaugural issue of the Caoye Weekly was published on May 4th, and it has been published weekly ever since, with increasing circulation. The Hangzhou branch was established on September 15th of last year, headed by Mr. Fan Dajun, and the society's affairs there are also unusually thriving. Each week, it sells over 700 copies of the Caoye Weekly from the head office. On April 10th of this year, it added a branch publication, the "Wild Grass Weekly." Due to the large number of society members in Shanghai and the heavy workload, the head, Mr. Jin Kuansheng, has established a local branch office at No. 33 Nanlu Lane, next door to the Ming Garden on Huade Road. Society members and readers in Shanghai East can inquire about anything, apply for membership, or subscribe from 12:00 noon to 2:00 PM and after 5:00 PM every day at the branch office. Everything is exactly the same as at the Fairen Road head office. A Shanghai West office will soon be established near the Jing'an Temple in Shanghai West to further expand the society's affairs. The head office's business hours are from 11:30 AM to 1:00 PM daily, and it is open all day on Sundays.

Guidelines for Youth Garden Contributions 105

(1) Articles should focus on discussions about youth issues, news about domestic and foreign schools or students, essays, and descriptions of school life, etc., in any style.

(2) Drawings are limited to those concerning youth issues.

(3) Photographs of youth life (such as sports, travel, excursions, drama performances, speeches, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements are acceptable, whether individual or group.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(5) Each article should not exceed two thousand characters.

(6) Do not write horizontally, and do not write carelessly. Western text should be avoided if possible; if it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not draw with blue ink or use colored paper for drawings; use only white paper and black ink.

(8) Please indicate that submissions are to be sent to the "Youth Garden Editorial Department".
